Title: Timeline of gravitational physics and relativity

URL Source: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity

Published Time: 2002-06-22T08:12:10Z

Markdown Content:
From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia

[![Image 1](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/E_mc_2_IMG_0859.jpg/330px-E_mc_2_IMG_0859.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:E_mc_2_IMG_0859.jpg)

Einstein's mass-energy equation in a 1912 manuscript. He originally used ![Image 2: {\displaystyle L}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/103168b86f781fe6e9a4a87b8ea1cebe0ad4ede8) instead of ![Image 3: {\displaystyle E}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4232c9de2ee3eec0a9c0a19b15ab92daa6223f9b) to denote energy.

The following is a **[timeline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline "Timeline") of [gravitational physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_physics "Gravitational physics") and [general relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_relativity "General relativity")**.

*   3rd century B.C. – [Aristarchus of Samos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aristarchus_of_Samos "Aristarchus of Samos") proposes the [heliocentric model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heliocentrism "Heliocentrism").[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:9-1)

*   1543 – [Nicolaus Copernicus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus "Nicolaus Copernicus") publishes [_On the Revolutions of Heavenly Spheres_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_revolutionibus_orbium_coelestium "De revolutionibus orbium coelestium").[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:9-1)
*   1583 – [Galileo Galilei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galileo_Galilei "Galileo Galilei") deduces the period relationship of a [pendulum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pendulum "Pendulum") from observations (according to later biographer).
*   1586 – [Simon Stevin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_Stevin "Simon Stevin") demonstrates that two objects of different mass accelerate at the same rate when dropped.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-2)
*   1589 – Galileo Galilei describes a [hydrostatic balance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrostatic_balance "Hydrostatic balance") for measuring [specific gravity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Specific_gravity "Specific gravity").
*   1590 – Galileo Galilei formulates modified [Aristotelean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aristotle "Aristotle") theory of motion (later retracted) based on [density](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Density "Density") rather than weight of objects.

[![Image 4](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Principia1846-105.png/250px-Principia1846-105.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Principia1846-105.png)

Geometric diagram for Newton's proof of Kepler's second law.

*   1602-1608 – Galileo Galilei experiments with pendulum motion and [inclined planes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inclined_plane "Inclined plane"); deduces his law of [free fall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_fall "Free fall"); and discovers that [projectiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Projectile "Projectile") travel along [parabolic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parabola "Parabola") trajectories.[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:11-3)
*   1609 – [Johannes Kepler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johannes_Kepler "Johannes Kepler") announces his first two [laws of planetary motion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kepler%27s_laws_of_planetary_motion "Kepler's laws of planetary motion").[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:8-4)
*   1610 – Johannes Kepler states the [dark night paradox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olbers%27s_paradox "Olbers's paradox").[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-5)
*   1610 – Galileo Galilei publishes _[The Sidereal Messenger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidereus\_Nuncius "Sidereus Nuncius")_, detailing his astronomical discoveries made with a telescope.[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-6)
*   1619 – Johannes Kepler unveils his third law of planetary motion.[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:8-4)
*   1665-66 – [Isaac Newton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Newton "Isaac Newton") introduces an inverse-square [law of universal gravitation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newton%27s_law_of_universal_gravitation "Newton's law of universal gravitation") uniting terrestrial and celestial theories of motion and uses it to predict the orbit of the [Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon "Moon") and the parabolic arc of projectiles (the latter using his [generalization of the binomial theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binomial_series "Binomial series")).[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:10-7)
*   1673 – [Christiaan Huygens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christiaan_Huygens "Christiaan Huygens") publishes his _[The Pendulum Clock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horologium\_Oscillatorium "Horologium Oscillatorium")_, describing the motion of [pendulums](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pendulum "Pendulum") and the formula for centripetal acceleration during [uniform circular motion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circular_motion#Uniform_circular_motion "Circular motion"), known to Isaac Newton since the 1660s.[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:18-8): 14 
*   1676-9 – [Ole Rømer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ole_R%C3%B8mer "Ole Rømer") makes the first scientific determination of the [speed of light](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speed_of_light "Speed of light").[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-9)
*   1684 – Isaac Newton proves that [planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planet "Planet") moving under an inverse-square force law will obey [Kepler's laws](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kepler%27s_laws "Kepler's laws") in [a letter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_motu_corporum_in_gyrum "De motu corporum in gyrum") to Edmond Halley.[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:10-7)
*   1686 – Isaac Newton uses a fixed length pendulum with weights of varying composition to test the [weak equivalence principle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weak_equivalence_principle "Weak equivalence principle") to 1 part in 1000.[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:7-10)[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-11)
*   1686 – Isaac Newton publishes his _[Mathematical Principles of Natural Philosophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophi%C3%A6\_Naturalis\_Principia\_Mathematica "Philosophiæ Naturalis Principia Mathematica")_, where he develops his [calculus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fluxion "Fluxion"), states his [laws of motion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newton%27s_laws_of_motion "Newton's laws of motion") and gravitation, proves the [shell theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shell_theorem "Shell theorem"), describes his [rotating bucket](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bucket_argument "Bucket argument") thought experiment, explains the [tides](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tidal_force "Tidal force"), and calculates the [figure of the Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Figure_of_the_Earth "Figure of the Earth").[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:7-10)

[![Image 5](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Lagrange_very_massive.svg/250px-Lagrange_very_massive.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lagrange_very_massive.svg)

Lagrange points

*   1705 – [Edmond Halley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edmond_Halley "Edmond Halley") predicts the return of [Halley's comet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Halley%27s_Comet "Halley's Comet") in 1758,[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-12) the first use of Newton's laws by someone other than Newton himself.[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-13)
*   1728 – Isaac Newton posthumously publishes his [cannonball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newton%27s_cannonball "Newton's cannonball") thought experiment.[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-treatiselat-14)[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-cohen2004-15)
*   1742 – [Colin Maclaurin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colin_Maclaurin "Colin Maclaurin") studies a self-gravitating uniform liquid drop at [equilibrium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrostatic_equilibrium "Hydrostatic equilibrium"), the [Maclaurin spheroid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maclaurin_spheroid "Maclaurin spheroid").[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-16)[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-17)
*   1740s – [Jean le Rond d'Alembert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_le_Rond_d%27Alembert "Jean le Rond d'Alembert") and [Leonhard Euler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonhard_Euler "Leonhard Euler") independently examine the [precession of the equinoxes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axial_precession "Axial precession") and [nutation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nutation "Nutation") of the Earth. In the process, they develop the dynamics of [rigid bodies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rigid_body "Rigid body").[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:16-18)
*   1740s-1750s – Leonhard Euler and [Alexis Clairault](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexis_Clairaut "Alexis Clairaut") independently derive the equations of motion for the [three-body problem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Three-body_problem "Three-body problem") and apply them to the Moon.[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:16-18)
*   1755 – [Immanuel Kant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immanuel_Kant "Immanuel Kant") advances [Emanuel Swedenborg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emanuel_Swedenborg "Emanuel Swedenborg")'s nebular hypothesis on the origin of the [Solar System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System "Solar System").[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Woolfson1993-19)
*   1765 – Leonhard Euler discovers the first three Lagrange points.[[20]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-20)[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-E327-21)
*   1767 – Leonhard Euler solves Euler's [restricted three-body problem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euler%27s_three-body_problem "Euler's three-body problem").[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-euler_1760-22)
*   1772 – [Joseph-Louis Lagrange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph-Louis_Lagrange "Joseph-Louis Lagrange") discovers the two remaining [Lagrange points](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lagrange_point "Lagrange point").[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-gallica.bnf.fr2-23)
*   1770s – [Pierre-Simon de Laplace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre-Simon_de_Laplace "Pierre-Simon de Laplace") develops [equations for the tides](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theory_of_tides#Laplace's_tidal_equations "Theory of tides") that take into account both gravitation and rotation.[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:18-8): 216 
*   1770s-1780s – Joseph-Louis Lagrange and Pierre-Simon de Laplace investigate the stability of the Solar System.[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:16-18)
*   1780s – [Adrien-Marie Legendre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adrien-Marie_Legendre "Adrien-Marie Legendre") and Pierre-Simon de Laplace study the gravitational attraction of [spheroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spheroid "Spheroid") in [spherical coordinates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spherical_coordinate_system "Spherical coordinate system") and introduce the [Legendre polynomials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legendre_polynomials "Legendre polynomials").[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:16-18)
*   1796 – Pierre-Simon de Laplace independently introduces the [nebular hypothesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nebular_hypothesis "Nebular hypothesis").[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Woolfson1993-19)
*   1798 – [Henry Cavendish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Cavendish "Henry Cavendish") tests Newton's law of universal gravitation using a [torsion balance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cavendish_experiment "Cavendish experiment"), leading to the first accurate value for the [gravitational constant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_constant "Gravitational constant") and the mean density of the Earth.[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-24)[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-25)
*   1799-1825 – Pierre-Simon de Laplace publishes his _[Treatise on Celestial Mechanics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trait%C3%A9\_de\_m%C3%A9canique\_c%C3%A9leste "Traité de mécanique céleste")_, in five volumes.[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:18-8): 216 

*   1846 – [Urbain Le Verrier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urbain_Le_Verrier "Urbain Le Verrier") and [John Couch Adams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Couch_Adams "John Couch Adams"), studying [Uranus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uranus "Uranus")' orbit, independently prove that another, farther planet must exist. [Neptune](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neptune "Neptune") was found at the predicted moment and position.
*   1855 – Le Verrier observes a 38 [arc-second](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arcsecond "Arcsecond") per century excess [precession](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precession "Precession") of [Mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_(planet) "Mercury (planet)")'s [orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbit "Orbit") and attributes it to another planet, inside Mercury's orbit. The planet, called [Vulcan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulcan_(hypothetical_planet) "Vulcan (hypothetical planet)"), was never found. Le Verrier's figure is revised by [Simon Newcomb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_Newcomb "Simon Newcomb") to 43 arc-second per century in 1882.[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:16-18)
*   1876 – [William Kingdon Clifford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Kingdon_Clifford "William Kingdon Clifford") suggests that the motion of matter may be due to changes in the geometry of space.[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-26)
*   1884 – William Thomson ([Lord Kelvin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lord_Kelvin "Lord Kelvin")) lectures on the issues with the wave theory of light with regards to the [luminiferous ether](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luminiferous_aether "Luminiferous aether").[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:15-27)
*   1887 – [Albert A. Michelson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_A._Michelson "Albert A. Michelson") and [Edward W. Morley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_W._Morley "Edward W. Morley") in [their famous experiment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment "Michelson–Morley experiment") do not detect the ether drift.[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-28)[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-29)
*   1889 – [Loránd Eötvös](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lor%C3%A1nd_E%C3%B6tv%C3%B6s "Loránd Eötvös") uses a [torsion balance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Torsion_spring#Torsion_balance "Torsion spring") to test the [weak equivalence principle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weak_equivalence_principle "Weak equivalence principle") to 1 part in one billion.[[30]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-30)
*   1887 – [George Francis FitzGerald](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Francis_FitzGerald "George Francis FitzGerald") explains his hypothesis that the Michelson-Morley interferometer [contracts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fitzgerald-Lorentz_contraction "Fitzgerald-Lorentz contraction") in the direction of motion through the [luminiferous ether](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luminiferous_aether "Luminiferous aether") to [Oliver Lodge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oliver_Lodge "Oliver Lodge").[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:15-27)
*   1893 – [Ernst Mach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernst_Mach "Ernst Mach") states [Mach's principle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mach%27s_principle "Mach's principle"), the first constructive critique of the idea of Newtonian absolute space.
*   1897 – [Henri Poincaré](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henri_Poincar%C3%A9 "Henri Poincaré") questions whether absolute space, absolute time, and [Euclidean geometry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euclidean_geometry "Euclidean geometry") are applicable to physics.[[31]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-31)

[![Image 6](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/USS_Enterprise_%28CVAN-65%29%2C_USS_Long_Beach_%28CGN-9%29_and_USS_Bainbridge_%28DLGN-25%29_underway_in_the_Mediterranean_Sea_during_Operation_Sea_Orbit%2C_in_1964.jpg/250px-USS_Enterprise_%28CVAN-65%29%2C_USS_Long_Beach_%28CGN-9%29_and_USS_Bainbridge_%28DLGN-25%29_underway_in_the_Mediterranean_Sea_during_Operation_Sea_Orbit%2C_in_1964.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:USS_Enterprise_(CVAN-65),_USS_Long_Beach_(CGN-9)_and_USS_Bainbridge_(DLGN-25)_underway_in_the_Mediterranean_Sea_during_Operation_Sea_Orbit,_in_1964.jpg)

The U.S. Navy's nuclear-powered Task Force 1 underway for [Operation Sea Orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Sea_Orbit "Operation Sea Orbit") in the Mediterranean, 1964.

*   1902 – [Paul Gerber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Gerber "Paul Gerber") explains the movement of the perihelion of Mercury using finite [speed of gravity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speed_of_gravity "Speed of gravity").[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-32) His formula, at least approximately, matches the later model from Einstein's general relativity, but Gerber's theory was incorrect.
*   1902 – Henri Poincaré questions the concept of [simultaneity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relativity_of_simultaneity "Relativity of simultaneity") in his book, _[Science and Hypothesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science\_and\_Hypothesis "Science and Hypothesis")_.[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:12-33)[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-34)
*   1904 – [Hendrik Antoon Lorentz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hendrik_Antoon_Lorentz "Hendrik Antoon Lorentz") publishes the [Lorentz transformations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lorentz_transformation "Lorentz transformation"),[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-35) so named by Henri Poincaré.[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:15-27)
*   1902 – Henri Poincaré shows that the Lorentz transformations form a [mathematical group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Group_(mathematics) "Group (mathematics)"), called the [Lorentz group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lorentz_group "Lorentz group"), and derives the [relativistic formula for adding velocities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Velocity-addition_formula "Velocity-addition formula").[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:15-27)
*   1905 – [Albert Einstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein "Albert Einstein") completes his [special theory of relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_relativity "Special relativity")[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-36)[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:82-37) and examines [relativistic aberration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relativistic_aberration "Relativistic aberration") and the [transverse Doppler effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transverse_Doppler_effect "Transverse Doppler effect").[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:15-27)
*   1905 – Albert Einstein discovers the [equivalence of mass and energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence "Mass–energy equivalence"),[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-38)![Image 7: {\displaystyle E=mc^{2}}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9f73dbd37a0cac34406ee89057fa1b36a1e6a18e) in modern form.[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-39)[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-40)[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:12-33)
*   1906 – [Max Planck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_Planck "Max Planck") coins the term _Relativtheorie_. Albert Einstein later uses the term _Relativitätstheorie_ in a conversation with Paul Ehrenfest. He originally prefers calling it Invariance Theory.[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-41)
*   1906 – Max Planck formulates a [variational principle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variational_principle "Variational principle") for special relativity.[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-42)
*   1907 – Albert Einstein introduces the [principle of equivalence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equivalence_principle "Equivalence principle") of gravitational and inertial mass and uses it to predict gravitational lensing and [gravitational redshift](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_redshift "Gravitational redshift"),[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-43)[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:22-44) historically known as the Einstein shift.[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:4-45)
*   1907-8 – [Hermann Minkowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermann_Minkowski "Hermann Minkowski") introduces the [Minkowski spacetime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minkowski_spacetime "Minkowski spacetime") and the notion of [tensors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tensor "Tensor") to relativity. His paper was published posthumously.[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-46)[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-47)[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-48)
*   1909 – [Max Born](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_Born "Max Born") proposes [his notion of rigidity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Born_rigidity "Born rigidity").[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-49)[[50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-50)
*   1909 – [Paul Ehrenfest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Ehrenfest "Paul Ehrenfest") states the [Ehrenfest paradox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ehrenfest_paradox "Ehrenfest paradox").[[51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-51)[[52]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-52)

[![Image 8](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Einstein%27s_argument_that_falling_light_acquires_energy.svg/250px-Einstein%27s_argument_that_falling_light_acquires_energy.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Einstein%27s_argument_that_falling_light_acquires_energy.svg)

Einstein's 1911 argument for gravitational redshift

*   1911 – [Max von Laue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_von_Laue "Max von Laue") publishes the first textbook on special relativity.[[53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:14-53)
*   1911 – Albert Einstein explains the need to replace both special relativity and Newton's theory of gravity; he realizes that the principle of equivalence only holds locally, not globally.[[54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-54)
*   1912 – [Friedrich Kottler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_Kottler "Friedrich Kottler") applies the notion of tensors to curved spacetime.[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-55)[[53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:14-53)
*   1915-16 – Albert Einstein completes his [general theory of relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_relativity "General relativity").[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-56)[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:13-57) He explains the [perihelion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perihelion "Perihelion") of Mercury and calculates [gravitational lensing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_lens "Gravitational lens") correctly and introduces the [post-Newtonian approximation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-Newtonian_expansion "Post-Newtonian expansion").[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-58)[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-59)
*   1915 – [David Hilbert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Hilbert "David Hilbert") independently introduces the [Einstein-Hilbert action](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%E2%80%93Hilbert_action "Einstein–Hilbert action").[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-60)[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:13-57) Hilbert also recognizes the connection between the Einstein equations and the [Gauss-Bonnet theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gauss%E2%80%93Bonnet_theorem "Gauss–Bonnet theorem").[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-61)
*   1916 – [Karl Schwarzschild](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Schwarzschild "Karl Schwarzschild") publishes the [Schwarzschild metric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schwarzschild_metric "Schwarzschild metric") about a month after Einstein published his general theory of relativity.[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-62)[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-63) This was the first solution to the Einstein field equations other than the trivial flat space solution.[[64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Levy-64)[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Eisenstaedt,_1989-65)[[66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-66)
*   1916 – Albert Einstein predicts [gravitational waves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_wave "Gravitational wave").[[67]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-67)
*   1916 – [Willem de Sitter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Willem_de_Sitter "Willem de Sitter") predicts the [geodetic effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geodetic_effect "Geodetic effect").[[68]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-68)
*   1917 – Albert Einstein applies his field equations to the entire Universe.[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-69)[Physical cosmology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physical_cosmology "Physical cosmology") is born.[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:22-44)
*   1916-20 – [Arthur Eddington](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Eddington "Arthur Eddington") studies the internal constitution of the stars.[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-eddington-70)[[71]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-eddington2-71)
*   1918 – Albert Einstein derives the [quadrupole formula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quadrupole_formula "Quadrupole formula") for gravitational radiation.[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-72)[[73]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-73)
*   1918 – [Emmy Noether](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emmy_Noether "Emmy Noether") publishes [Noether's theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noether%27s_theorem "Noether's theorem") and resolves the issue of local [energy conservation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservation_of_energy "Conservation of energy") in general relativity.[[74]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-74)[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-75)
*   1918 – [Josef Lense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josef_Lense "Josef Lense") and [Hans Thirring](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_Thirring "Hans Thirring") find the [gravitomagnetic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitoelectromagnetism "Gravitoelectromagnetism")[frame-dragging](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frame-dragging "Frame-dragging") of [gyroscopes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gyroscope "Gyroscope") in the equations of general relativity.[[76]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-76)[[77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-77)[[78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-78)
*   1919 – Arthur Eddington leads a [solar eclipse expedition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eddington_experiment "Eddington experiment") which detects gravitational deflection of light by the Sun,[[79]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Eddington1920-79) which, despite opinion to the contrary, survives modern scrutiny.[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-PhysToday-80) Other teams fail for reasons of [war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I") and politics.[[81]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-81)

*   1921 – [Theodor Kaluza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theodor_Kaluza "Theodor Kaluza") demonstrates that a [five-dimensional version of Einstein's equations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaluza%E2%80%93Klein_theory "Kaluza–Klein theory") unifies [gravitation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitation "Gravitation") and [electromagnetism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetism "Electromagnetism").[[82]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-kal-82) This idea is later extended by [Oskar Klein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oskar_Klein "Oskar Klein").[[83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-83)
*   1922 – [Alexander Friedmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Friedmann "Alexander Friedmann") derives the [Friedmann equations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedmann_equations "Friedmann equations").[[84]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-af1922-84)[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:22-44)
*   1922 – [Enrico Fermi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enrico_Fermi "Enrico Fermi") introduces the [Fermi coordinates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fermi_coordinates "Fermi coordinates").[[85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-85)[[86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-86) This is developed further in 1932 by Arthur Walker into the [Fermi-Walker transport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fermi%E2%80%93Walker_transport "Fermi–Walker transport").[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:02-87)
*   1923 – [George David Birkhoff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_David_Birkhoff "George David Birkhoff") proves [Birkhoff's theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Birkhoff%27s_theorem_(relativity) "Birkhoff's theorem (relativity)") on the uniqueness of the Schwarzschild solution.
*   1924 – Arthur Eddington calculates the [Eddington limit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eddington_luminosity "Eddington luminosity").[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-eddington3-88)
*   1924 – [Cornelius Lanczos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cornelius_Lanczos "Cornelius Lanczos") discovers the [van Stockum dust](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Van_Stockum_dust "Van Stockum dust"),[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-89) later rediscovered by [Willem Jacob van Stockum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Willem_Jacob_van_Stockum "Willem Jacob van Stockum") in 1938.[[90]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-90)
*   1925 – [Walter Adams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_Sydney_Adams "Walter Sydney Adams") measures the gravitational redshift of the light emitted by the companion of Sirius B, a [white dwarf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_dwarf "White dwarf").[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-91)
*   1927 – [Georges Lemaître](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georges_Lema%C3%AEtre "Georges Lemaître") publishes his hypothesis of the [primeval atom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_Bang "Big Bang").[[92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-92)[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:22-44)
*   1929 – [Edwin Hubble](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edwin_Hubble "Edwin Hubble") published the [law later named for him](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hubble%27s_Law "Hubble's Law").[[93]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-hubble-93)

[![Image 9](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Einstein_cross_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Einstein_cross_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Einstein_cross_(cropped).jpg)

The [Einstein Cross](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein_Cross "Einstein Cross") is an example of gravitational lensing at work. This one was discovered in 1985.[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-94)

*   1931 – [Subrahmanyan Chandrasekhar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subrahmanyan_Chandrasekhar "Subrahmanyan Chandrasekhar") studies the [stability](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chandrasekhar_limit "Chandrasekhar limit") of [white dwarfs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_dwarf "White dwarf").[[95]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-chandra3-95)[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-chandra4-96)
*   1931 – Georges Lemaître and Arthur Eddington predict the [expansion of the Universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expansion_of_the_universe "Expansion of the universe").[[97]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-97)[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-98)
*   1931 – Albert Einstein introduces his [cosmological constant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmological_constant "Cosmological constant").[[99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-99)
*   1932 – Albert Einstein and Willem de Sitter propose the [Einstein-de Sitter cosmological model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%E2%80%93de_Sitter_universe "Einstein–de Sitter universe").[[100]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-100)
*   1932 – [John Cockcroft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Cockcroft "John Cockcroft") and [Ernest Walton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernest_Walton "Ernest Walton") verify Einstein's mass-energy equation by an experiment artificially [transmuting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_transmutation "Nuclear transmutation") lithium into helium.[[101]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-101)[[102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-102)
*   1934 – [Dmitry Blokhintsev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dmitry_Blokhintsev "Dmitry Blokhintsev") and F. M. Gal'perin coin the term '[graviton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graviton "Graviton")'.[[103]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-103)[Paul Dirac](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Dirac "Paul Dirac") reintroduces it in 1959.[[104]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-104)[[105]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Debnath-105)
*   1934 – [Walter Baade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_Baade "Walter Baade") and [Fritz Zwicky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fritz_Zwicky "Fritz Zwicky") predict the existence of [neutron stars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neutron_star "Neutron star").[[106]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-106) Although their details are wrong, their basic idea is now accepted.[[107]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-107)
*   1935 – Albert Einstein and [Nathan Rosen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nathan_Rosen "Nathan Rosen") derive the [Einstein-Rosen bridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wormhole "Wormhole"), the first wormhole solution.[[108]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-ER-108)
*   1935 – [Howard Robertson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Howard_P._Robertson "Howard P. Robertson") and [Arthur Walker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Geoffrey_Walker "Arthur Geoffrey Walker") obtain the [Robertson-Walker metric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robertson-Walker_metric "Robertson-Walker metric").[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:02-87)
*   1936 – Albert Einstein predicts that a gravitational lens brightens the light coming from a distant object to the observer.[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-109)
*   1937 – Fritz Zwicky states that [galaxies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galaxy "Galaxy") could act as [gravitational lenses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_lens "Gravitational lens").[[110]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-110)
*   1937 – Albert Einstein and Nathan Rosen obtain the [Einstein-Rosen metric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein-Rosen_metric "Einstein-Rosen metric"), the first exact solution describing gravitational waves.[[111]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-111)
*   1938 – Albert Einstein, Leopold Infeld, and Banesh Hoffmann obtain the [Einstein-Infeld-Hoffmann equations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%E2%80%93Infeld%E2%80%93Hoffmann_equations "Einstein–Infeld–Hoffmann equations") of motion.[[112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-112)
*   1939 – [Hans Bethe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_Bethe "Hans Bethe") shows that nuclear fusion is responsible for energy production inside stars,[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-frs-113) building upon the [Kelvin–Helmholtz mechanism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kelvin%E2%80%93Helmholtz_mechanism "Kelvin–Helmholtz mechanism").
*   1939 – [Richard Tolman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_C._Tolman "Richard C. Tolman") solves the Einstein field equations in the case of a spherical fluid drop.[[114]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-114)[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:6-115)
*   1939 – [Robert Serber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Serber "Robert Serber"), [George Volkoff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Volkoff "George Volkoff"), [Richard Tolman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_C._Tolman "Richard C. Tolman"), and J. Robert Oppenheimer study the stability of neutron stars, obtaining the [Tolman–Oppenheimer–Volkoff limit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tolman%E2%80%93Oppenheimer%E2%80%93Volkoff_limit "Tolman–Oppenheimer–Volkoff limit").[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-116)[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-117)[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:6-115)
*   1939 – [J. Robert Oppenheimer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._Robert_Oppenheimer "J. Robert Oppenheimer") and [Hartland Snyder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hartland_Snyder "Hartland Snyder") publish the [Oppenheimer-Snyder model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oppenheimer%E2%80%93Snyder_model "Oppenheimer–Snyder model") for the continued gravitational contraction of a star.[[118]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-118)[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:6-115)[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-119)

*   1948 – [Ralph Alpher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ralph_Alpher "Ralph Alpher") and [Robert Herman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Herman "Robert Herman") predict the [cosmic microwave background](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmic_microwave_background "Cosmic microwave background").[[120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-120)[[121]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-121)
*   1949 – [Cornelius Lanczos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cornelius_Lanczos "Cornelius Lanczos") introduces the [Lanczos potential](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lanczos_tensor "Lanczos tensor") for the [Weyl tensor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weyl_tensor "Weyl tensor").[[122]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Lanczos1949-122)
*   1949 – [Kurt Gödel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurt_G%C3%B6del "Kurt Gödel") discovers [Gödel's solution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%B6del_metric "Gödel metric").[[123]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-123)

*   1953 – [P. C. Vaidya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/P._C._Vaidya "P. C. Vaidya") Newtonian time in general relativity, Nature, **171**, p260.
*   1954 – [Suraj Gupta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suraj_N._Gupta "Suraj N. Gupta") sketches how to derive the equations of general relativity from quantum field theory for a massless spin-2 particle (the [graviton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graviton "Graviton")).[[124]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-PPS-124) His procedure was later carried out by [Stanley Deser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanley_Deser "Stanley Deser") in 1970.[[125]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-125)[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Preskill-126)
*   1955-56 – [Robert Kraichnan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Kraichnan "Robert Kraichnan") shows that under the appropriate assumptions, Einstein's field equations of gravitation arise from the [quantum field theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_field_theory "Quantum field theory") of a massless spin-2 particle coupled to the stress-energy tensor.[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-127)[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-128) This follows from his unpublished work as an undergraduate in 1947.[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Preskill-126)
*   1956 – [Bruno Berlotti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bruno_Bertotti "Bruno Bertotti") develops the [post-Minkowskian expansion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-Minkowskian_expansion "Post-Minkowskian expansion").[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-129)
*   1956 – [John Lighton Synge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Lighton_Synge "John Lighton Synge") publishes the first relativity text emphasizing [spacetime diagrams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minkowski_diagram "Minkowski diagram") and [geometrical methods](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geometrical_methods&action=edit&redlink=1 "Geometrical methods (page does not exist)").
*   1957 – [Felix A. E. Pirani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Felix_A._E._Pirani "Felix A. E. Pirani") uses [Petrov classification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petrov_classification "Petrov classification") to understand [gravitational radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_radiation "Gravitational radiation").
*   1957 – [Richard Feynman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Feynman "Richard Feynman") introduces his [sticky bead argument](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sticky_bead_argument "Sticky bead argument").[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Preskill-126)[[130]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Feynman-130) He later derives the quadrupole formula in a letter to [Victor Weisskopf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victor_Weisskopf "Victor Weisskopf") (1961).[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Preskill-126)
*   1957-8 – [John Wheeler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Archibald_Wheeler "John Archibald Wheeler") discusses the breakdown of classical general relativity near [singularities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_singularity "Gravitational singularity") and the need for [quantum gravity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_gravity "Quantum gravity").[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:22-44)
*   1958 – [David Finkelstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Finkelstein "David Finkelstein") presents [a new coordinate system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eddington-Finkelstein_coordinates "Eddington-Finkelstein coordinates") that eliminates the Schwarzschild radius as a singularity.[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-131)
*   1959 – [Robert Pound](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Pound "Robert Pound") and [Glen Rebka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glen_Rebka "Glen Rebka") propose the [Pound–Rebka experiment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pound%E2%80%93Rebka_experiment "Pound–Rebka experiment"), first precision test of [gravitational redshift](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_redshift "Gravitational redshift"). The experiment relies on the [Mössbauer effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M%C3%B6ssbauer_effect "Mössbauer effect").[[132]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-132)
*   1959 – Lluís Bel introduces [Bel–Robinson tensor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bel%E2%80%93Robinson_tensor "Bel–Robinson tensor") and the [Bel decomposition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bel_decomposition "Bel decomposition") of the [Riemann tensor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Riemann_tensor "Riemann tensor").
*   1959 – [Arthur Komar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Komar "Arthur Komar") introduces the [Komar mass](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Komar_mass "Komar mass").
*   1959 – [Richard Arnowitt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Arnowitt "Richard Arnowitt"), Stanley Deser and [Charles W. Misner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_W._Misner "Charles W. Misner") developed [ADM formalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ADM_formalism "ADM formalism").

*   1960 – [Martin Kruskal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_Kruskal "Martin Kruskal") and [George Szekeres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Szekeres "George Szekeres") independently introduce the [Kruskal–Szekeres coordinates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kruskal%E2%80%93Szekeres_coordinates "Kruskal–Szekeres coordinates") for the [Schwarzschild vacuum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schwarzschild_vacuum "Schwarzschild vacuum").[[133]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-133)[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-rsbm-134)
*   1960 – John Graves and Dieter Brill study the causal structure of [an electrically charged black hole](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reissner%E2%80%93Nordstr%C3%B6m_metric "Reissner–Nordström metric").[[135]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-135)
*   1960 – Thomas Matthews and [Allan R. Sandage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allan_R._Sandage "Allan R. Sandage") associate [3C 48](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/3C_48 "3C 48") with a point-like optical image, show radio source can be at most 15 light minutes in diameter,
*   1960 – [Ivor M. Robinson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ivor_Robinson_(physicist) "Ivor Robinson (physicist)") and [Andrzej Trautman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrzej_Trautman "Andrzej Trautman") discover the Robinson-Trautman [null dust solution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Null_dust_solution "Null dust solution")[[136]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-RobTrautmanPhysRevL1960_fixthis-136)
*   1960 – Robert Pound and Glen Rebka test the gravitational redshift predicted by the equivalence principle to approximately 1%.[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-137)
*   1961 –[Tullio Regge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tullio_Regge "Tullio Regge") introduces the [Regge calculus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regge_calculus "Regge calculus").[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-138)
*   1961 – [Carl H. Brans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_H._Brans "Carl H. Brans") and [Robert H. Dicke](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_H._Dicke "Robert H. Dicke") introduce [Brans–Dicke theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brans%E2%80%93Dicke_theory "Brans–Dicke theory"), the first viable alternative theory with a clear physical motivation.[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-139)
*   1961 – [Pascual Jordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascual_Jordan "Pascual Jordan") and [Jürgen Ehlers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Ehlers "Jürgen Ehlers") develop the _kinematic decomposition_ of a [timelike congruence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timelike_congruence "Timelike congruence"),
*   1961 – Robert Dicke, Peter Roll, and R. Krotkov refine the [Eötvös experiment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/E%C3%B6tv%C3%B6s_experiment "Eötvös experiment") to an accuracy of 10−11.[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-140)[[141]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-141)
*   1962 – John Wheeler and Robert Fuller show that the Einstein-Rosen bridge is unstable.[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-142)
*   1962 – [Roger Penrose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Penrose "Roger Penrose") and [Ezra T. Newman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ezra_T._Newman "Ezra T. Newman") introduce the [Newman–Penrose formalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newman%E2%80%93Penrose_formalism "Newman–Penrose formalism").
*   1962 – Ehlers and [Wolfgang Kundt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolfgang_Kundt "Wolfgang Kundt") classify the symmetries of [Pp-wave spacetimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pp-wave_spacetimes "Pp-wave spacetimes").
*   1962 –[Joshua Goldberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joshua_N._Goldberg "Joshua N. Goldberg") and [Rainer K. Sachs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rainer_K._Sachs "Rainer K. Sachs") prove the [Goldberg–Sachs theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goldberg%E2%80%93Sachs_theorem "Goldberg–Sachs theorem").[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-original_paper-143)
*   1962 – Ehlers introduces [Ehlers transformations](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ehlers_transformation&action=edit&redlink=1 "Ehlers transformation (page does not exist)"), a new [solution generating method](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Solution_generating_method&action=edit&redlink=1 "Solution generating method (page does not exist)"),
*   1962 – [Richard Arnowitt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Arnowitt "Richard Arnowitt"), [Stanley Deser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanley_Deser "Stanley Deser"), and Charles W. Misner introduce the [ADM reformulation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ADM_formalism "ADM formalism") and [global hyperbolicity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_hyperbolicity "Global hyperbolicity"),
*   1962 – Istvan Ozsvath and [Englbert Schücking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Englbert_Sch%C3%BCcking "Englbert Schücking") rediscover the [circularly polarized monochromomatic gravitational wave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ozv%C3%A1th-Sch%C3%BCcking_metric "Ozváth-Schücking metric").
*   1962 – [Hans Adolph Buchdahl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_Adolph_Buchdahl "Hans Adolph Buchdahl") discovers [Buchdahl's theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buchdahl%27s_theorem "Buchdahl's theorem").
*   1962 – [Hermann Bondi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermann_Bondi "Hermann Bondi") introduces [Bondi mass](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bondi_mass "Bondi mass").
*   1962 – [Hermann Bondi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermann_Bondi "Hermann Bondi"), M. G. van der Burg, A. W. Metzner, and [Rainer K. Sachs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rainer_K._Sachs "Rainer K. Sachs") introduce the [asymptotic symmetry group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bondi%E2%80%93Metzner%E2%80%93Sachs_group "Bondi–Metzner–Sachs group") of [asymptotically flat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asymptotically_flat_spacetime "Asymptotically flat spacetime"), Lorentzian spacetimes at null (_i.e._, light-like) infinity.
*   1963 – [Roy Kerr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roy_Kerr "Roy Kerr") discovers the [Kerr vacuum solution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerr_metric "Kerr metric") of [Einstein's field equations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%27s_field_equations "Einstein's field equations"),[[144]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-kerr_1963-144)
*   1963 – Redshifts of [3C 273](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/3C_273 "3C 273") and other quasars show they are very distant; hence very luminous,
*   1963 – Newman, T. Unti and L.A. Tamburino introduce the [NUT vacuum solution](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=NUT_vacuum_solution&action=edit&redlink=1 "NUT vacuum solution (page does not exist)"),
*   1963 – [Roger Penrose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Penrose "Roger Penrose") introduces [Penrose diagrams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penrose_diagram "Penrose diagram") and [Penrose limits](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Penrose_limit&action=edit&redlink=1 "Penrose limit (page does not exist)").[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-145)
*   1963 – [Maarten Schmidt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maarten_Schmidt "Maarten Schmidt") and [Jesse Greenstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesse_L._Greenstein "Jesse L. Greenstein") discover quasi-stellar objects, later shown to be moving away from Earth due to the expansion of the Universe.[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:22-44)
*   1963 – First [Texas Symposium on Relativistic Astrophysics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ivor_Robinson_(physicist)#Texas_Symposium_on_Relativistic_Astrophysics "Ivor Robinson (physicist)") held in Dallas, 16–18 December.[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:22-44)
*   1964 – [Steven Weinberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steven_Weinberg "Steven Weinberg") shows that a quantum field theory of interacting massless spin-2 particles is Lorentz invariant only if it satisfies the principle of equivalence.[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-146)[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-147)[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Preskill-126)
*   1964 – [Subrahmanyan Chandrasekhar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subrahmanyan_Chandrasekhar "Subrahmanyan Chandrasekhar") determines a stability criterion.[[148]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-148)
*   1964 – R. W. Sharp and Charles Misner introduce the [Misner–Sharp mass](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Misner%E2%80%93Sharp_mass&action=edit&redlink=1 "Misner–Sharp mass (page does not exist)").
*   1964 – [Hong-Yee Chiu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hong-Yee_Chiu "Hong-Yee Chiu") coins the term "'[quasar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quasar "Quasar")" for quasi-stellar radio sources.[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-149)
*   1964 – [Sjur Refsdal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sjur_Refsdal "Sjur Refsdal") suggests that the Hubble constant could be determined using gravitational lensing.[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-150)
*   1964 – [Irwin Shapiro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irwin_Shapiro "Irwin Shapiro") predicts a [gravitational time delay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shapiro_effect "Shapiro effect") of radiation travel as a test of general relativity.[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Shapiro1964-151)[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-152)
*   1965 – Roger Penrose proves the first [singularity theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penrose%E2%80%93Hawking_singularity_theorems "Penrose–Hawking singularity theorems").[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-153)[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:22-44)
*   1965 – Penrose discovers the structure of the light cones in [gravitational plane wave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_plane_wave "Gravitational plane wave") spacetimes.
*   1965 – [Ezra Newman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ezra_T._Newman "Ezra T. Newman") and others introduce [Kerr-Newman metric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerr%E2%80%93Newman_metric "Kerr–Newman metric").[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-154)[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-155)
*   1965 – [Arno Penzias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arno_Penzias "Arno Penzias") and [Robert Wilson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Woodrow_Wilson "Robert Woodrow Wilson") accidentally discover the [cosmic microwave background radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmic_microwave_background_radiation "Cosmic microwave background radiation").[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-156) This rules out the [steady-state model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steady-state_model "Steady-state model") of [Fred Hoyle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fred_Hoyle "Fred Hoyle") and [Jayant Narlikar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jayant_Narlikar "Jayant Narlikar").[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:22-44)
*   1965 – [Joseph Weber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Weber "Joseph Weber") puts the first Weber bar [gravitational wave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_wave "Gravitational wave") detector into operation.
*   1966 – Sachs and [Ronald Kantowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Kantowski "Ronald Kantowski") discover the [Kantowski-Sachs dust solution](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kantowski-Sachs_dust_solution&action=edit&redlink=1 "Kantowski-Sachs dust solution (page does not exist)").
*   1967 – John Archibald Wheeler popularizes "black hole" at a conference.[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:6-115)[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-157)
*   1967 – [Jocelyn Bell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jocelyn_Bell "Jocelyn Bell") and [Antony Hewish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antony_Hewish "Antony Hewish") discover [pulsars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pulsars "Pulsars").[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:1-158)
*   1967 – [Robert H. Boyer](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Robert_H._Boyer&action=edit&redlink=1 "Robert H. Boyer (page does not exist)") and [R. W. Lindquist](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=R._W._Lindquist&action=edit&redlink=1 "R. W. Lindquist (page does not exist)") introduce [Boyer–Lindquist coordinates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boyer%E2%80%93Lindquist_coordinates "Boyer–Lindquist coordinates") for the Kerr vacuum.
*   1967 – [Bryce DeWitt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bryce_DeWitt "Bryce DeWitt") publishes on canonical quantum gravity.[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-159)
*   1967 – [Werner Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Werner_Israel "Werner Israel") proves a special case of the [no-hair theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No-hair_theorem "No-hair theorem") and the converse of Birkhoff's theorem.[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-160)
*   1967 – [Kenneth Nordtvedt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kenneth_Nordtvedt "Kenneth Nordtvedt") develops [PPN formalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PPN_formalism "PPN formalism").
*   1967 – [Mendel Sachs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mendel_Sachs "Mendel Sachs") publishes factorization of Einstein's field equations.
*   1967 – [Hans Stephani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_Stephani "Hans Stephani") discovers the [Stephani dust solution](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Stephani_dust_solution&action=edit&redlink=1 "Stephani dust solution (page does not exist)").
*   1968 – [F. J. Ernst](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=F._J._Ernst&action=edit&redlink=1 "F. J. Ernst (page does not exist)") discovers the [Ernst equation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernst_equation "Ernst equation").
*   1968 – [B. Kent Harrison](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=B._Kent_Harrison&action=edit&redlink=1 "B. Kent Harrison (page does not exist)") discovers the [Harrison transformation](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Harrison_transformation&action=edit&redlink=1 "Harrison transformation (page does not exist)"), a solution-generating method.
*   1968 – [Brandon Carter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brandon_Carter "Brandon Carter") solves the geodesic equations for Kerr–Newmann electrovacuum with [Carter's constant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carter_constant "Carter constant").[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-carter_1968-161)
*   1968 – [Hugo D. Wahlquist](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hugo_D._Wahlquist&action=edit&redlink=1 "Hugo D. Wahlquist (page does not exist)") discovers the [Wahlquist fluid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wahlquist_fluid "Wahlquist fluid").
*   1968 – [James Hartle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Hartle "James Hartle") and [Kip Thorne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kip_Thorne "Kip Thorne") obtain the [Hartle–Thorne metric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hartle%E2%80%93Thorne_metric "Hartle–Thorne metric").[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-162)
*   1968 – Irwin Shapiro and his colleagues present the first detection of the Shapiro delay.[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Shapiro1968-163)
*   1968 – [Kenneth Nordtvedt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kenneth_Nordtvedt "Kenneth Nordtvedt") studies [a possible violation of the weak equivalence principle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nordtvedt_effect "Nordtvedt effect") for self-gravitating bodies and proposes a new test of the weak equivalence principle based on observing the relative motion of the Earth and Moon in the Sun's gravitational field.[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-164)
*   1969 – [William B. Bonnor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_B._Bonnor "William B. Bonnor") introduces the [Bonnor beam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bonnor_beam "Bonnor beam").[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-165)
*   1969 – [Joseph Weber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Weber "Joseph Weber") reports observation of [gravitational waves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_waves "Gravitational waves")[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-166) a claim now generally discounted.[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Science_Magazine-167)[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-168)
*   1969 – Penrose proposes the (weak) [cosmic censorship hypothesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmic_censorship_hypothesis "Cosmic censorship hypothesis") and the [Penrose process](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penrose_process "Penrose process"),[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-169)
*   1969 – Misner introduces the [mixmaster universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mixmaster_universe "Mixmaster universe").
*   1969 – [Yvonne Choquet-Bruhat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yvonne_Choquet-Bruhat "Yvonne Choquet-Bruhat") and [Robert Geroch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Geroch "Robert Geroch") discuss global aspects of the [Cauchy problem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cauchy_problem "Cauchy problem") in general relativity.[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-170)
*   1965-70 – Subrahmanyan Chandrasekhar and colleagues develops the [post-Newtonian expansions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-Newtonian_expansion "Post-Newtonian expansion").[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-171)[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-172)[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-173)[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-174)[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-175)
*   1968-70 – Roger Penrose, [Stephen Hawking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_Hawking "Stephen Hawking"), and [George Ellis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_F._R._Ellis "George F. R. Ellis") prove that singularities must arise in the Big Bang models.[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-176)[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-177)

*   1970 – [Vladimir Alekseevich Belinski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Belinski "Vladimir Belinski"), [Isaak Markovich Khalatnikov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaak_Markovich_Khalatnikov "Isaak Markovich Khalatnikov"), and [Evgeny Lifshitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evgeny_Lifshitz "Evgeny Lifshitz") introduce the [BKL conjecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BKL_conjecture "BKL conjecture"). 

Using a hammer and a feather, Scott validates [Galileo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galileo "Galileo")'s claim that objects in a vacuum will fall at the same rate.

*   1970 – Stephen Hawking and Roger Penrose prove trapped surfaces must arise in black holes.
*   1971 – [David Scott](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Scott "David Scott") demonstrates that a hammer and a feather fall at the same rate on the Moon.[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:11-3)
*   1971 – Alfred Goldhaber and Michael Nieto give stringent limits on the photon mass.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-178) The strictest one is ![Image 10: {\displaystyle m_{\gamma }\leq 4\times 10^{-51}{\text{kg}}}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e9f659db7c0aeaa685717bf67c98a5c98f0cc0dc).[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-179)
*   1971 – Stephen Hawking proves that the area of a black hole can never decrease.[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-180)[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:22-44)
*   1971 – [Peter C. Aichelburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_C._Aichelburg "Peter C. Aichelburg") and [Roman U. Sexl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_U._Sexl "Roman U. Sexl") introduce the [Aichelburg–Sexl ultraboost](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aichelburg%E2%80%93Sexl_ultraboost "Aichelburg–Sexl ultraboost").
*   1971 – Introduction of the [Khan–Penrose vacuum](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Khan%E2%80%93Penrose_vacuum&action=edit&redlink=1 "Khan–Penrose vacuum (page does not exist)"), a simple explicit colliding plane wave spacetime.
*   1971 – [Robert H. Gowdy](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Robert_H._Gowdy&action=edit&redlink=1 "Robert H. Gowdy (page does not exist)") introduces the [Gowdy vacuum solutions](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gowdy_vacuum_solutions&action=edit&redlink=1 "Gowdy vacuum solutions (page does not exist)") (cosmological models containing circulating gravitational waves).[![Image 11](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Chandra_image_of_Cygnus_X-1.jpg/250px-Chandra_image_of_Cygnus_X-1.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Chandra_image_of_Cygnus_X-1.jpg)

Image of Cygnus X-1 by the [Chandra X-ray Observatory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chandra_X-ray_Observatory "Chandra X-ray Observatory") (2009)

*   1971 – [Cygnus X-1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cygnus_X-1 "Cygnus X-1"), the first solid black hole candidate, discovered by [Uhuru satellite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uhuru_(satellite) "Uhuru (satellite)").[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:22-44)
*   1971 – [William H. Press](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_H._Press "William H. Press") discovers black hole [ringing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ringing_(signal) "Ringing (signal)") by [numerical simulation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_relativity "Numerical relativity").
*   1971 – Harrison and Estabrook algorithm for solving systems of PDEs.
*   1971 – [James W. York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_W._York "James W. York") introduces [conformal method](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Conformal_method&action=edit&redlink=1 "Conformal method (page does not exist)") generating initial data for ADM initial value formulation.
*   1971 – [Robert Geroch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Geroch "Robert Geroch") introduces [Geroch group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geroch_group "Geroch group") and a [solution generating method](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Solution_generating_method&action=edit&redlink=1 "Solution generating method (page does not exist)").
*   1972 – [Jacob Bekenstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacob_Bekenstein "Jacob Bekenstein") proposes that black holes have a non-decreasing [entropy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Entropy "Entropy") which can be identified with the area.[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-181)[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:22-44)
*   1972 – Sachs introduces [optical scalars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optical_scalars "Optical scalars") and proves [peeling theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peeling_theorem "Peeling theorem").
*   1972 – [Rainer Weiss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rainer_Weiss "Rainer Weiss") proposes concept of interferometric gravitational wave detector in an unpublished manuscript.[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-182)
*   1972 – [Joseph Hafele](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_C._Hafele "Joseph C. Hafele") and [Richard Keating](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_E._Keating "Richard E. Keating") perform the [Hafele–Keating experiment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hafele%E2%80%93Keating_experiment "Hafele–Keating experiment").[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-paper1-183)[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-paper2-184)[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-New_Scientist_1972-185)
*   1972 – [Richard H. Price](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_H._Price "Richard H. Price") studies [gravitational collapse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_collapse "Gravitational collapse") with numerical simulations.
*   1972 – [Saul Teukolsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saul_Teukolsky "Saul Teukolsky") derives the [Teukolsky equation](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Teukolsky_equation&action=edit&redlink=1 "Teukolsky equation (page does not exist)").[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-186)
*   1972 – [Yakov B. Zel'dovich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yakov_B._Zel%27dovich "Yakov B. Zel'dovich") predicts the transmutation of electromagnetic and gravitational radiation.
*   1972 – Brandon Carter, Stephen Hawking, and [James M. Bardeen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_M._Bardeen "James M. Bardeen") propose the four [laws of black hole mechanics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laws_of_black_hole_mechanics "Laws of black hole mechanics").[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-187)[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:22-44)
*   1972 – James Bardeen calculates the [shadow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shadow "Shadow") of a black hole.[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-188) This was later verified by the Event Horizon Telescope.[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-189)
*   1973 – [Charles W. Misner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_W._Misner "Charles W. Misner"), [Kip S. Thorne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kip_S._Thorne "Kip S. Thorne") and [John A. Wheeler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_A._Wheeler "John A. Wheeler") publish the treatise _[Gravitation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitation\_(book) "Gravitation (book)")_, a textbook that remains in use in the twenty-first century.[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-190)[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-191)
*   1973 – [Stephen W. Hawking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_W._Hawking "Stephen W.
