Hawking") and [George Ellis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Francis_Rayner_Ellis "George Francis Rayner Ellis") publish the monograph _[The Large Scale Structure of Space-Time](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Large\_Scale\_Structure\_of\_Space-Time "The Large Scale Structure of Space-Time")_.[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:22-44)
*   1973 – Robert Geroch introduces the [GHP formalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GHP_formalism "GHP formalism").
*   1973 – Homer Ellis obtains the [Ellis drainhole](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ellis_drainhole "Ellis drainhole"),[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-ellis12-192) the first traversable wormhole.
*   1974 – [Russell Hulse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russell_Hulse "Russell Hulse") and [Joseph Hooton Taylor, Jr.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Hooton_Taylor,_Jr. "Joseph Hooton Taylor, Jr.") discover the [Hulse–Taylor binary pulsar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PSR_1913%2B16 "PSR 1913+16"),
*   [![Image 12: Computer simulation of a black hole accretion disk published in 1979 by Jean-Pierre Luminet](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/BH-JPL-A%26A1979.jpg/250px-BH-JPL-A%26A1979.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:BH-JPL-A%26A1979.jpg)

Computer simulation of a black hole accretion disk published in 1979 by Jean-Pierre Luminet

1974 – [James W. York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_W._York "James W. York") and Niall Ó Murchadha present the analysis of the initial value formulation and examine the stability of its solutions.
*   1974 – R. O. Hansen introduces [Hansen–Geroch multipole moments](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hansen%E2%80%93Geroch_multipole_moment&action=edit&redlink=1 "Hansen–Geroch multipole moment (page does not exist)").
*   1974 – Stephen Hawking discovers [Hawking radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawking_radiation "Hawking radiation").[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-193)[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-194)
*   1975 – Stephen Hawking shows that [the area of a black hole is proportional to its entropy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bekenstein-Hawking_entropy_equation "Bekenstein-Hawking entropy equation"), as previously conjectured by Jacob Bekenstein.[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-195)
*   1975 – Roberto Colella, [Albert Overhauser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Overhauser "Albert Overhauser"), and Samuel Werner observe the quantum-mechanical phase shift of neutrons due to gravity.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-196)[Neutron interferometry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neutron_interferometer "Neutron interferometer") was later used to test the principle of equivalence.[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-197)[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-198)[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-199)
*   1975 – Chandrasekhar and [Steven Detweiler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steven_Detweiler "Steven Detweiler") compute the effects of perturbations on a Schwarzschild black hole.[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-200)
*   1975 – Szekeres and D. A. Szafron discover the [Szekeres–Szafron dust solutions](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Szekeres%E2%80%93Szafron_dust_solutions&action=edit&redlink=1 "Szekeres–Szafron dust solutions (page does not exist)").
*   1976 – Penrose introduces [Penrose limits](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Penrose_limit&action=edit&redlink=1 "Penrose limit (page does not exist)") (every null geodesic in a Lorentzian spacetime behaves like a plane wave),
*   1978 – Penrose introduces the notion of a _thunderbolt_,
*   1978 – Belinskiǐ and Zakharov show how to solve [Einstein's field equations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%27s_field_equations "Einstein's field equations") using the [inverse scattering transform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inverse_scattering_transform "Inverse scattering transform"); the first [gravitational solitons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_soliton "Gravitational soliton"),
*   1979 – [Dennis Walsh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dennis_Walsh "Dennis Walsh"), [Robert Carswell](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Robert_Carswell_(scientist)&action=edit&redlink=1 "Robert Carswell (scientist) (page does not exist)"), and [Ray Weymann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_Weymann "Ray Weymann") discover the gravitationally lensed [quasar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quasar "Quasar")[Q0957+561](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Q0957%2B561 "Q0957+561").[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-201)
*   1979 – [Jean-Pierre Luminet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Luminet "Jean-Pierre Luminet") creates an image of a black hole with an [accretion disk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accretion_disk "Accretion disk") using computer simulation.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-202)[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-203)
*   1979 – Steven Detweiler proposes using [pulsar timing arrays](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pulsar_timing_array "Pulsar timing array") to detect gravitational waves.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-DetweilerPulsarTiming-204)
*   1979-81 – [Richard Schoen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Schoen "Richard Schoen") and [Shing-Tung Yau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shing-Tung_Yau "Shing-Tung Yau") prove the [positive mass theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Positive_energy_theorem "Positive energy theorem").[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-205)[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-206)[Edward Witten](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Witten "Edward Witten") independently proves the same thing.[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-207)

[![Image 13: Variations in the temperature of the cosmic microwave background measured by the COBE satellite.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/COBE_cmb_fluctuations.png/250px-COBE_cmb_fluctuations.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:COBE_cmb_fluctuations.png)

Variations in the temperature of the cosmic microwave background measured by the COBE satellite. The plane of the Milky Way Galaxy is horizontal across the middle of each picture.

*   1980 – [Vera Rubin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vera_Rubin "Vera Rubin") and colleagues study the rotational properties of [UGC 2885](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UGC_2885 "UGC 2885"), demonstrating the prevalence of dark matter.[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-208)[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-209)
*   1980 – [Gravity Probe A](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravity_Probe_A "Gravity Probe A") verifies gravitational redshift to approximately 0.007% using a space-born [hydrogen maser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrogen_maser "Hydrogen maser").[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-210)
*   1980 – James Bardeen explains structure in the Universe using [cosmological perturbation theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmological_perturbation_theory "Cosmological perturbation theory").[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-211)
*   1981 – [Alan Guth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Guth "Alan Guth") proposes [cosmic inflation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inflation_(cosmology) "Inflation (cosmology)") in order to solve the [flatness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flatness_problem "Flatness problem") and [horizon problems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horizon_problem "Horizon problem").[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-212)
*   1982 – [Joseph Taylor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Hooton_Taylor,_Jr. "Joseph Hooton Taylor, Jr.") and [Joel Weisberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Joel_Weisberg&action=edit&redlink=1 "Joel Weisberg (page does not exist)") show that the rate of energy loss from the binary [pulsar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pulsar "Pulsar")[PSR B1913+16](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PSR_B1913%2B16 "PSR B1913+16") agrees with that predicted by the general relativistic [quadrupole formula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quadrupole_formula "Quadrupole formula") to within 5%.[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-tw82-213)
*   1983 – James Hartle and Stephen Hawking propose the [no-boundary wave function](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hartle%E2%80%93Hawking_state "Hartle–Hawking state") for the Universe.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-214)[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:22-44)
*   1983-84 – [RELIKT-1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RELIKT-1 "RELIKT-1") observes the cosmic microwave background.
*   1986 – Helmut Friedrich proves that the [de Sitter spacetime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_Sitter_space "De Sitter space") is stable.[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-215)[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:0-216)
*   1986 – [Bernard Schutz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bernard_F._Schutz "Bernard F. Schutz") shows that cosmic distances can be determined using sources of gravitational waves without references to the [cosmic distance ladder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmic_distance_ladder "Cosmic distance ladder").[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-217) Standard-siren astronomy is born.
*   1988 – [Mike Morris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Morris_(physicist) "Mike Morris (physicist)"), Kip Thorne, and [Yurtsever Ulvi](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Yurtsever_Ulvi&action=edit&redlink=1 "Yurtsever Ulvi (page does not exist)") obtain the [Morris-Thorne wormhole](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morris-Thorne_wormhole "Morris-Thorne wormhole").[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-218) Morris and Thorne argue for its pedagogical value.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-219)
*   1989 – [Steven Weinberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steven_Weinberg "Steven Weinberg") discusses the [cosmological constant problem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmological_constant_problem "Cosmological constant problem"), the discrepancy between the measured value and those predicted by modern theories of elementary particles.[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-220)
*   1989-93 – The [Cosmic Background Explorer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmic_Background_Explorer "Cosmic Background Explorer") (COBE) identifies anisotropy in the cosmic microwave background.[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-221)[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-222)

[![Image 14](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/GR2bodyparameterspace.png/330px-GR2bodyparameterspace.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:GR2bodyparameterspace.png)

Parameter space of various approximation techniques in general relativity

*   1992 – Stephen Hawking states his [chronology protection conjecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chronology_protection_conjecture "Chronology protection conjecture").[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-223)
*   1993 – [Demetrios Christodoulou](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demetrios_Christodoulou "Demetrios Christodoulou") and [Sergiu Klainerman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergiu_Klainerman "Sergiu Klainerman") prove the non-linear stability of the [Minkowski spacetime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minkowski_space "Minkowski space").[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-224)[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:0-216)
*   1995 – John F. Donoghue show that general relativity is a quantum [effective field theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Effective_field_theory "Effective field theory").[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-225) This framework could be used to analyze binary systems observed by gravitational-wave observatories.[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-226)
*   1995 – [Hubble Deep Field](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hubble_Deep_Field "Hubble Deep Field") image taken.[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Hubble_image-227) It is a landmark in the study of cosmology.
*   1998 – The first complete [Einstein ring](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein_ring "Einstein ring"), [B1938+666](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=B1938%2B666&action=edit&redlink=1 "B1938+666 (page does not exist)"), discovered using the [Hubble Space Telescope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope "Hubble Space Telescope") and [MERLIN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MERLIN "MERLIN").[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Bullseye-228)[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-229)
*   1998-99 – Scientists discover that the expansion of the Universe is [accelerating](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accelerating_expansion_of_the_universe "Accelerating expansion of the universe").[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-230)[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-231)
*   1999 – [Alessandra Buonanno](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alessandra_Buonanno "Alessandra Buonanno") and [Thibault Damour](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thibault_Damour "Thibault Damour") introduce the [effective one-body formalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Effective_one-body_formalism "Effective one-body formalism").[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-232) This was later used to analyze data collected by gravitational-wave observatories.[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-233)

*   2003 – Arvind Borde, [Alan Guth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Guth "Alan Guth"), and [Alexander Vilenkin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Vilenkin "Alexander Vilenkin") prove the [Borde–Guth–Vilenkin theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Borde%E2%80%93Guth%E2%80%93Vilenkin_theorem "Borde–Guth–Vilenkin theorem").[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-234)[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Cosmocurious-235)
*   2002 – First data collection of the [Laser Interferometer Gravitational-Wave Observatory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LIGO "LIGO") (LIGO).
*   2002 – James Williams, Slava Turyshev, and Dale Boggs conduct stringent lunar test of violations of the principle of equivalence.[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-236)
*   2005 – Daniel Holz and Scott Hughes coin the term "standard sirens".[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-237)
*   2009 – [Gravity Probe B](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravity_Probe_B "Gravity Probe B") experiment verifies the geodetic effect to 0.5%.[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-238)[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-PRL-239)

[![Image 15](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/PIA16874-CobeWmapPlanckComparison-20130321.jpg/330px-PIA16874-CobeWmapPlanckComparison-20130321.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:PIA16874-CobeWmapPlanckComparison-20130321.jpg)

Improving cosmological measurements by three different satellites

*   2010 – A team at the U.S. [National Institute for Standards and Technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Institute_of_Standards_and_Technology "National Institute of Standards and Technology") (NIST) verifies relativistic time dilation using optical [atomic clocks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_clock "Atomic clock").[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-240)[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-241)
*   2011 – [Wilkinson Microwave Anisotropy Probe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilkinson_Microwave_Anisotropy_Probe "Wilkinson Microwave Anisotropy Probe") (WMAP) finds no statistically significant deviations from the [ΛCDM model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lambda-CDM_model "Lambda-CDM model") of cosmology.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-WMAP_CMB-242)
*   2012 – [Hubble Ultra-Deep Field](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hubble_Ultra-Deep_Field "Hubble Ultra-Deep Field") image released. It was created using data collected by the Hubble Space Telescope between 2003 and 2004.[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-xdf-243)
*   2013 – [NuSTAR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NuSTAR "NuSTAR") and [XMM-Newton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XMM-Newton "XMM-Newton") measure the spin of the [supermassive black hole](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supermassive_black_hole "Supermassive black hole") at the center of the galaxy [NGC 1365](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NGC_1365 "NGC 1365").[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-244)
*   2015 – Advanced LIGO reports the first direct detections of gravitational waves, [GW150914](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GW150914 "GW150914")[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-245) and [GW151226](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GW151226 "GW151226"),[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-PRL-20160615-246) mergers of stellar-mass black holes. [Gravitational-wave astronomy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational-wave_astronomy "Gravitational-wave astronomy") is born.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Naeye-247) No deviations from general relativity were found.[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-248)[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-MIT-249)
*   2017 – [LIGO-VIRGO collaboration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LIGO-Virgo_Collaboration "LIGO-Virgo Collaboration") detects gravitational waves emitted by a neutron-star binary, [GW170817](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GW170817 "GW170817").[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:3-250) The [Fermi Gamma-ray Space Telescope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fermi_Gamma-ray_Space_Telescope "Fermi Gamma-ray Space Telescope") and the International Gamma-ray Astrophysics Laboratory ([INTEGRAL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/INTEGRAL "INTEGRAL")) unambiguously detect the corresponding gamma-ray burst.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:5-251)[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-252) LIGO-VIRGO and Fermi constrain the difference between the speed of gravity and the speed of light in vacuum to 10−15.[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Abbott^3_AJT-253) This marks the first time electromagnetic and gravitational waves are detected from a single source,[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-254)[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-255) and give direct evidence that some (short) gamma-ray bursts are due to colliding neutron stars.[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:3-250)[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:5-251)
*   2017 – [Multi-messenger astronomy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multi-messenger_astronomy "Multi-messenger astronomy") reveals neutron-star mergers to be responsible for the [nucleosynthesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleosynthesis "Nucleosynthesis") of some heavy elements,[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-SM-20171016-256)[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-NASA-20171016-257)[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-258)[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-259) such as [strontium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strontium "Strontium"),[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-260) via the rapid-neutron capture or [r-process](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/R-process "R-process").[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-261)
*   2017 – [MICROSCOPE](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MICROSCOPE "MICROSCOPE") satellite experiment verifies the principle of equivalence to 10−15 in terms of the Eötvös ratio ![Image 16: {\displaystyle \eta }](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e4d701857cf5fbec133eebaf94deadf722537f64).[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Touboul2017-262) The final report is published in 2022.[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-263)[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-264)
*   2017 – Principle of equivalence tested to 10−9 for atoms in a [coherent state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coherent_state "Coherent state") of [superposition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_superposition "Quantum superposition").[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-265)
*   2017 – Scientists begin using gravitational-wave sources as "[standard sirens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_sirens "Standard sirens")" to measure the Hubble constant, finding its value to be broadly in line with the best estimates of the time.[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-266)[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Nat24471-267) Refinements of this technique will help resolve [discrepancies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hubble%27s_law#Hubble_tension "Hubble's law") between the different methods of measurements.[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-NAT-20181017-268)
*   2017 – [Neutron Star Interior Composition Explorer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neutron_Star_Interior_Composition_Explorer "Neutron Star Interior Composition Explorer") (NICER) arrives on the International Space Station.[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:1-158)
*   2017-18 – Georgios Moschidis proves the instability of the [anti-de Sitter spacetime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-de_Sitter_space "Anti-de Sitter space").[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:0-216)
*   2018 – Final paper by the [Planck satellite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planck_(spacecraft) "Planck (spacecraft)") collaboration.[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-planck2018-269) Planck operated between 2009 and 2013.
*   2018 – Mihalis Dafermos and Jonathan Luk disprove the strong cosmic censorship hypothesis for the Cauchy horizon of an uncharged, rotating black hole.[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-270)
*   2018 – [European Southern Observatory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Southern_Observatory "European Southern Observatory") (ESO) observes gravitational redshift of radiation emitted by matter orbiting [Sagittarius A*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sagittarius_A* "Sagittarius A*"), the central supermassive black hole of the Milky Way,[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-271) and verifies the [innermost stable circular orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Innermost_stable_circular_orbit "Innermost stable circular orbit") for that object.[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-272)
*   2018 – Advanced LIGO-VIRGO collaboration constrains [equations of state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equations_of_state "Equations of state") for a neutron star using GW170817.[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-273)[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-274)
*   2018 – Luciano Rezzolla, Elias R. Most, and Lukas R. Weih used gravitational-wave data from GW170817 constrain the possible maximum mass for a neutron star to around 2.17 solar masses.[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Rezzolla2018-275)
*   2018 – Kris Pardo, Maya Fishbach, Daniel Holz, and David Spergel limit the number of spacetime dimensions through which gravitational waves can propagate to 3 + 1, in line with general relativity and ruling out models that allow for "leakage" to higher dimensions of space.[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-arxiv.org_2-276)[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-277) Analyses of GW170817 have also ruled out many other alternatives to general relativity,[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-278)[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-279)[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-280)[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-281) and proposals for dark energy.[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Dark_Energy_after_GW_170817-282)[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-283)[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Dark_Energy_After_GW170817:_Dead_En-284)[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-285)[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-286)
*   2018 – Two different experimental teams report highly precise values of Newton's gravitational constant ![Image 17: {\displaystyle G}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f5f3c8921a3b352de45446a6789b104458c9f90b) that slightly disagree.[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-287)[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-288)[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-289)
*   2019 – [Event Horizon Telescope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Event_Horizon_Telescope "Event Horizon Telescope") (EHT) releases an image of [supermassive black hole](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supermassive_black_hole "Supermassive black hole")[M87*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Messier_87#Supermassive_black_hole_M87* "Messier 87"), and measures its mass and shadow.[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-290)[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-291) Results are confirmed in 2024.[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-292)
*   2019 – Advanced LIGO and VIRGO detect [GW190814](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GW190814 "GW190814"), the collision of a 26-solar-mass black hole and a 2.6-solar-mass object, either an extremely heavy neutron star or a very light black hole.[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-LIGO-2020-293)[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-AJL-20200623-294) This is the largest mass gap seen in a gravitational-wave source to-date.

[![Image 18](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Eso2208-eht-mwe.tif/lossy-page1-280px-Eso2208-eht-mwe.tif.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Eso2208-eht-mwe.tif)

The size of Sagittarius A* is smaller than the orbit of [Mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_(planet) "Mercury (planet)").

*   2020 – Principle of equivalence tested for individual atoms using [atomic interferometry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atom_interferometer "Atom interferometer") to ~10−12.[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-295)[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-296)
*   2020 – ESO observes [Schwarzschild precession](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apsidal_precession#General_relativity "Apsidal precession") of the star [S2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S2_(star) "S2 (star)") about Sagittarius A*.[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-297)
*   2021 – [Jun Ye](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jun_Ye "Jun Ye") and his team measure gravitational redshift with an accuracy of 7.6 × 10−21 using an [ultracold](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultracold_atom "Ultracold atom") cloud of 100,000 strontium atoms in an [optical lattice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optical_lattice "Optical lattice").[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-298)[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-299)
*   2021 – EHT measures the polarization of the ring of M87*,[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-300) and other properties of the magnetic field in its vicinity.[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-301)
*   2021 – EHT releases an image of Sagittarius A*,[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-AJ-202205-302)[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-NYT-20220512-303) measures its shadow,[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-304) and shows that it is accurately described by the Kerr metric.[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-305)[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-306)
*   2022 – Chris Overstreet and his team observe the [gravitational Aharonov-Bohm effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_Aharonov-Bohm_effect "Gravitational Aharonov-Bohm effect")[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-307)[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-308)[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-309) using an experimental design from 2012.[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-310)[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-311)
*   2022 – [James Webb Space Telescope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Webb_Space_Telescope "James Webb Space Telescope") (JWST) publishes its first image, a [deep-field photograph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Webb%27s_First_Deep_Field "Webb's First Deep Field") of the [SMACS 0723](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SMACS_0723 "SMACS 0723") galaxy cluster.[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-312)
*   2022 – [Neil Gehrels Swift Observatory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neil_Gehrels_Swift_Observatory "Neil Gehrels Swift Observatory") detects [GRB 221009A](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GRB_221009A "GRB 221009A"), the brightest gamma-ray burst recorded.[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-313)[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:2-314)[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-NASA20221013-315)
*   2022 – JWST identifies several candidate high-redshift objects, corresponding to just a few hundred million years after the Big Bang.[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-MNRAS-20230101-316)[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-Yan2023-317)
*   2023 – James Nightingale and colleagues detect [Abell 1201](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abell_1201_BCG "Abell 1201 BCG"), an ultramassive black hole (33 billion solar masses), using strong gravitational lensing.[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-318)
*   2023 – Matteo Bachetti and colleagues confirm that neutron star [M82 X-2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M82_X-2 "M82 X-2") is violating the [Eddington limit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eddington_luminosity "Eddington luminosity"), making it an [ultraluminous X-ray source](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultraluminous_X-ray_source "Ultraluminous X-ray source") (ULX).[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-319)[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-320)
*   2023 – Team led by Dong Sheng and Zheng-Tian Lu found a [null result](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Null_result "Null result") for the coupling between quantum spin and gravity to 10−9.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-321)[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-322)
*   2023 – The [North American Nanohertz Observatory for Gravitational Waves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_American_Nanohertz_Observatory_for_Gravitational_Waves "North American Nanohertz Observatory for Gravitational Waves") (NANOGrav), the [European Pulsar Timing Array](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Pulsar_Timing_Array "European Pulsar Timing Array") (EPTA), the [Parkes Pulsar Timing Array](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parkes_Observatory "Parkes Observatory") (Australia), and the [Chinese Pulsar Timing Array](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Five-hundred-meter_Aperture_Spherical_Telescope "Five-hundred-meter Aperture Spherical Telescope") report detection of a [gravitational-wave background](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_wave_background "Gravitational wave background").[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-323)[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-324)[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-325)[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-326)[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-327)
*   2023 – [Geraint F. Lewis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geraint_F._Lewis "Geraint F. Lewis") and Brendon Brewer present evidence of cosmological time dilation in quasars.[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-328)[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-329)
*   2024 – The [Large High Altitude Air Shower Observatory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Large_High_Altitude_Air_Shower_Observatory "Large High Altitude Air Shower Observatory") (LHAASO) collaboration imposes stringent limits on violations of [Lorentz invariance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lorentz_invariance "Lorentz invariance") proposed in certain theories of [quantum gravity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_gravity "Quantum gravity") using GRB 221009A.[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-330)[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-331)
*   2024 – Álvaro Álvarez-Domínguez, Luis J. Garay, Eduardo Martín-Martínez, and José Polo-Gómez show that [quantum electrodynamics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_electrodynamics "Quantum electrodynamics") prevents a [kugelblitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kugelblitz_(astrophysics) "Kugelblitz (astrophysics)") from forming.[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-332)[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:03-333)[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_note-:17-334)

*   [Timeline of black hole physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_black_hole_physics "Timeline of black hole physics")
*   [Timeline of special relativity and the speed of light](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_special_relativity_and_the_speed_of_light "Timeline of special relativity and the speed of light")

149.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_gravitational_physics_and_relativity#cite_ref-149)**Chiu, Hong-Yee (May 1964). ["Gravitational collapse"](https://doi.org/10.1063%2F1.3051610). _Physics Today_. **17** (5): 21–34. [Bibcode](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bibcode_(identifier) "Bibcode (identifier)"):[1964PhT....17e..21C](https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/1964PhT....17e..21C). [doi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doi_(identifier) "Doi (identifier)"):[10.1063/1.3051610](https://doi.org/10.1063%2F1.3051610). So far, the clumsily long name 'quasi-stellar radio sources' is used to describe these objects. Because the nature of these objects is entirely unknown, it is hard to prepare a short, appropriate nomenclature for them so that their essential properties are obvious from their name. For convenience, the abbreviated form 'quasar' will be used throughout this paper.
